Will voters get to see the candidates before Nov. 3?</h1><div class=gnt_ar_by><a href=/staff/4388140002/luke-ramseth/ class="gnt_ar_by_a gnt_ar_by_a__fi">Luke Ramseth</a><div class=gnt_ar_pb>Mississippi Clarion Ledger</div></div><div class=gnt_ar_dt aria-label="Published 8:40 a.m. CT Oct. 15, 2020"></div><div class="gnt_ss gnt_ss__cm__tp" data-g-r=base_sc data-ss-u=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/2020/10/15/hyde-smith-declines-debate-espy-mississippi-senate-race/3643690001/ data-ss-t="Espy wants a debate. Hyde-Smith doesn't. Will voters get to see the candidates before Nov. 3?" data-ss-d="U.S. Sen. Cindy Hyde-Smith said only &#34;losing candidates and reporters&#34; care about debates. She's declined to accept invitations."><a class=gnt_ss_cm Cindy Hyde-Smith and Democrat Mike Espy greet each other before a televised debate in 2018. It does not appear the two will debate before their Nov. 3 rematch after Hyde-Smith has declined invitations."/><div class="gnt_em_img_ccw gnt_em_img_ccw__cap gnt_em_img_ccw__crd" data-c-caption="U.S. Sen. Cindy Hyde-Smith and Democrat Mike Espy greet each other before a televised debate in 2018. It does not appear the two will debate before their Nov. 3 rematch after Hyde-Smith has declined invitations." data-c-credit="Rogelio V. Solis, AP"></div></figure><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>A campaign season tradition — the candidate debate — almost certainly won't happen in the high-profile race between Republican U.S. Sen. Cindy Hyde-Smith and Democrat Mike Espy.</p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Hyde Smith told the Clarion Ledger on Wednesday she doesn't plan to debate, citing a busy schedule and "stark, drastic" differences between herself and Espy that she believes voters already know about.</p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>She similarly <a href=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/elections/2018/11/08/cindy-hyde-smith-agrees-debate-mike-espy-before-senate-runoff/1929551002/ target=_blank rel=noopener data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>declined to debate him and other challengers before her 2018 special election</a>, though eventually agreed to one before the runoff against Espy, which she won by about eight points. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>"To be honest with you, the debate about debates, that is something that losing candidates and reporters care about," Hyde-Smith said in a phone interview. She said Mississippians are more interested in the issues themselves, such as the economy and coronavirus response, not hearing about whether a debate will occur.</p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>At a news conference earlier in the day, Espy slammed Hyde-Smith for refusing to debate. </p><figure class="gnt_em gnt_em_img"><img class=gnt_em_img_i style=height:430px data-g-r=lazy data-gl-src="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2020/10/14/PJAM/7e7786c4-4ed8-44ce-9c71-58585ef2ac7f-SDW_5226.jpg?width=660&height=430&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp" data-gl-srcset="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2020/10/14/PJAM/7e7786c4-4ed8-44ce-9c71-58585ef2ac7f-SDW_5226.jpg?width=1320&height=860&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp 2x" decoding=async alt="Mike Espy, Democratic candidate for the U.S. Senate in Mississippi, speaks to media during a press conference at his campaign headquarters in Jackson, Miss. Wednesday, Oct. 14, 2020. During the press conference, Espy addressed his candidacy and Republican U.S. Senator Cindy Hyde-Smith's refusal to debate."/><div class="gnt_em_img_ccw gnt_em_img_ccw__cap gnt_em_img_ccw__crd" data-c-caption="Mike Espy, Democratic candidate for the U.S. Senate in Mississippi, speaks to media during a press conference at his campaign headquarters in Jackson, Miss. Wednesday, Oct. 14, 2020. During the press conference, Espy addressed his candidacy and Republican U.S. Senator Cindy Hyde-Smith's refusal to debate." data-c-credit="Eric Shelton/Clarion Ledger"></div></figure><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>"I think it is imperative that voters hear directly from Sen. Cindy Hyde-Smith, and directly from me, about where we stand on the important issues of Mississippi," Espy said, adding she is disrespecting Mississippi voters and "taking them for granted." </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p><strong class=gnt_ar_b_al>Their debate in 2018:</strong><a href=http://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/elections/2018/11/20/ms-sen-debate-what-cindy-hyde-smith-mike-espy-said-before-runoff/2012159002/ target=_blank rel=noopener data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>Scandals, health care, 'public hangings' and more: Key takeaways from #MSSen debate</a></p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>He said stark differences with Hyde-Smith is exactly why they should debate. "If you felt the same about views, programs or had a similar platform, you wouldn't have to debate anyone," Espy said. </p><aside aria-label=advertisement class="gnt_m gnt_x gnt_x__lbl gnt_x__al"><div data-g-r=lazy data-gl-method=lazyLoadX id=~ad-slot-7103-ms-jackson-C1098-native-article_link-news-politics-2 class="gnt_x_sl gnt_x_al"></div></aside><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Espy said the campaign received two debate invitations. A campaign spokeswoman said WJTV-TV and WLBT-TV both invited the candidates to separate debates. Espy agreed to a pair of dates, one in August and one in September, and said he is willing to attend one before Nov. 3. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p><strong>2019 </strong><a href=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/2019/06/13/mississippi-elections-why-do-top-governor-ag-candidates-dodge-debates/1418738001/ target=_blank rel=noopener data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a><strong>Debate dodgers:</strong> Top Mississippi candidates avoid debates. Why?</a></p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Hyde-Smith said the next few weeks are too busy. She said she will be back in Washington, D.C. early next week for much of the rest of the month due to the U.S. Supreme Court confirmation of Amy Coney Barrett. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>But Espy pointed out that other high-profile Senate Republicans had recently found time to debate their challengers — including Majority Leader Mitch McConnell of Kentucky, Lindsey Graham of South Carolina and Maine's Susan Collins.</p><figure class="gnt_em gnt_em_img"><img class=gnt_em_img_i style=height:529px data-g-r=lazy data-gl-src="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2018/11/07/PJAM/b1ce54b3-ea7a-4613-87fe-c8809f19551f-WickerHydeSMith.jpg?width=660&height=529&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp" data-gl-srcset="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2018/11/07/PJAM/b1ce54b3-ea7a-4613-87fe-c8809f19551f-WickerHydeSMith.jpg?width=1320&height=1058&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp 2x" decoding=async alt="U.S. senators Roger Wicker and Cindy Hyde-Smith celebrate with supporters of their campaigns at their shared election night party at the Westin hotel in downtown Jackson. Tuesday, Nov. 6, 2018."/><div class="gnt_em_img_ccw gnt_em_img_ccw__cap gnt_em_img_ccw__crd" data-c-caption="U.S. senators Roger Wicker and Cindy Hyde-Smith celebrate with supporters of their campaigns at their shared election night party at the Westin hotel in downtown Jackson. Tuesday, Nov. 6, 2018." data-c-credit="Sarah Warnock, Clarion Ledger"></div></figure><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Hyde-Smith argued she already debated Espy once in 2018, and little has changed since then regarding their positions. Voters are welcome to research her voting record, she said, both in the Senate and her previous stint in the Mississippi Legislature, to learn more about where she stands on issues. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>"I don't feel extremely compelled that the people of Mississippi think that it's really, really important," she said of a debate, adding it's "easy to see the differences" and labeling Espy as a liberal. She did not directly respond to a question about whether a debate might help voters better understand those policy differences. </p><aside aria-label=advertisement class="gnt_m gnt_x gnt_x__lbl gnt_x__al"><div data-g-r=lazy data-gl-method=lazyLoadX id=~ad-slot-7103-ms-jackson-C1098-native-article_link-news-politics-3 class="gnt_x_sl gnt_x_al"></div></aside><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Marvin King, an Ole Miss political science professor, said Hyde-Smith may fear giving Espy's campaign too much oxygen that could come along with a strong debate performance by him, or weak performance by her, so late in the race. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p><strong class=gnt_ar_b_al>Earlier:</strong><a href=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/2020/09/04/mississippi-senate-race-mike-espy-rally-stacey-abrams-jackson-church/5695664002/ target=_blank rel=noopener data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>Democrat Mike Espy holds first in-person rally of 2020 Senate campaign</a></p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>"It does deny swing voters — such that we have any in the state — the opportunity to see them on the same stage, answering the same questions," King said. </p><aside class="gnt_em gnt_em_anc" id=gnt_atomsnc data-g-r=lazy data-gl-method=loadAnc aria-label="Newsletter signup form"></aside><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Nathan Shrader, a Millsaps College political science professor, said it is highly unusual for a debate not to occur in a competitive Senate race. He said the sharply contrasting views Hyde-Smith described are the most important reason to hold a debate, because it allows the candidates to "lay that vision out, side by side." </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Shrader said Hyde-Smith may be generally uncomfortable with debating after the <a href=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/elections/2018/11/20/ms-sen-debate-what-cindy-hyde-smith-mike-espy-said-before-runoff/2012159002/ target=_blank rel=noopener data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>2018 event against Espy</a>, which he said did not go well for her. She departed without answering reporters' questions and instead sent her colleague, Sen. Roger Wicker, to speak with the press about her performance. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>"It's just not in her wheelhouse," Shrader said. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p><em>Contact Luke Ramseth at 601-961-7050 or <a href=mailto:lramseth@gannett.com data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>lramseth@gannett.com</a>. Follow <a href="https://twitter.com/lramseth?lang=en" data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>@lramseth</a> on Twitter.</em></p></div><div class=gnt_ss data-g-r=base_sc data-ss-u=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/2020/10/15/hyde-smith-declines-debate-espy-mississippi-senate-race/3643690001/ data-ss-t="Espy wants a debate. Hyde-Smith doesn't. Will voters get to see the candidates before Nov. 3?" data-ss-d="U.S. Sen. Cindy Hyde-Smith said only &#34;losing candidates and reporters&#34; care about debates. She's declined to accept invitations."><a class=gnt_ss_cm Hyde-Smith doesn't. Will voters get to see the candidates before Nov. 3?</h1><div class=gnt_ar_by><a href=/staff/4388140002/luke-ramseth/ class="gnt_ar_by_a gnt_ar_by_a__fi">Luke Ramseth</a><div class=gnt_ar_pb>Mississippi Clarion Ledger</div></div><div class=gnt_ar_dt aria-label="Published 8:40 a.m. CT Oct. 15, 2020"></div><div class="gnt_ss gnt_ss__cm__tp" data-g-r=base_sc data-ss-u=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/2020/10/15/hyde-smith-declines-debate-espy-mississippi-senate-race/3643690001/ data-ss-t="Espy wants a debate. USAT&#34;}],&#34;title&#34;:&#34;Man travels the US to mow lawns for those in need&#34;,&#34;url&#34;:&#34;/videos/life/humankind/2020/10/16/man-travels-us-mow-lawns-those-need/3678857001/&#34;}"></div><button class=gnt_em_vp_db aria-label="Close autoplay video player" data-t-l=${tc}|tealplayer|automated-playerClose><svg viewBox="0 0 16 16"><path d="M9 7.625L13.125 3.5 14.5 4.875 10.375 9l4.125 4.125-1.375 1.375L9 10.375 4.875 14.5 3.5 13.125 7.625 9 3.5 4.875 4.875 3.5 9 7.625z"/></svg></button><div class=teal-video-wrap><video poster="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2020/10/16/USAT/e8773f0b-f453-4883-92df-05fa2d373fe1-Courtesy_Rodney_Smith_Jr._16x9.jpg?width=660&height=371&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp" title="Man travels the US to mow lawns for those in need" muted playsinline elementtiming=avp-video></video></div></div></aside><div class=gnt_ar_b><figure class="gnt_em gnt_em__fp gnt_em_img"><img class=gnt_em_img_i style=height:420px src="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2018/11/21/PJAM/e8027986-679c-4269-b886-33dec346a67a-US_Senate_debate.jpg?width=660&height=420&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp" elementtiming=ar-lead-image srcset="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2018/11/21/PJAM/e8027986-679c-4269-b886-33dec346a67a-US_Senate_debate.jpg?width=1320&height=840&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp 2x" decoding=async alt="U.S. Sen. Cindy Hyde-Smith and Democrat Mike Espy greet each other before a televised debate in 2018. It does not appear the two will debate before their Nov. 3 rematch after Hyde-Smith has declined invitations."/><div class="gnt_em_img_ccw gnt_em_img_ccw__cap gnt_em_img_ccw__crd" data-c-caption="U.S. Sen. Cindy Hyde-Smith and Democrat Mike Espy greet each other before a televised debate in 2018. It does not appear the two will debate before their Nov. 3 rematch after Hyde-Smith has declined invitations." data-c-credit="Rogelio V. Solis, AP"></div></figure><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>A campaign season tradition — the candidate debate — almost certainly won't happen in the high-profile race between Republican U.S. Sen. Cindy Hyde-Smith and Democrat Mike Espy.</p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Hyde Smith told the Clarion Ledger on Wednesday she doesn't plan to debate, citing a busy schedule and "stark, drastic" differences between herself and Espy that she believes voters already know about.</p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>She similarly <a href=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/elections/2018/11/08/cindy-hyde-smith-agrees-debate-mike-espy-before-senate-runoff/1929551002/ target=_blank rel=noopener data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>declined to debate him and other challengers before her 2018 special election</a>, though eventually agreed to one before the runoff against Espy, which she won by about eight points. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>"To be honest with you, the debate about debates, that is something that losing candidates and reporters care about," Hyde-Smith said in a phone interview. She said Mississippians are more interested in the issues themselves, such as the economy and coronavirus response, not hearing about whether a debate will occur.</p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>At a news conference earlier in the day, Espy slammed Hyde-Smith for refusing to debate. </p><figure class="gnt_em gnt_em_img"><img class=gnt_em_img_i style=height:430px data-g-r=lazy data-gl-src="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2020/10/14/PJAM/7e7786c4-4ed8-44ce-9c71-58585ef2ac7f-SDW_5226.jpg?width=660&height=430&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp" data-gl-srcset="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2020/10/14/PJAM/7e7786c4-4ed8-44ce-9c71-58585ef2ac7f-SDW_5226.jpg?width=1320&height=860&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp 2x" decoding=async alt="Mike Espy, Democratic candidate for the U.S. Senate in Mississippi, speaks to media during a press conference at his campaign headquarters in Jackson, Miss. Wednesday, Oct. 14, 2020. During the press conference, Espy addressed his candidacy and Republican U.S. Senator Cindy Hyde-Smith's refusal to debate."/><div class="gnt_em_img_ccw gnt_em_img_ccw__cap gnt_em_img_ccw__crd" data-c-caption="Mike Espy, Democratic candidate for the U.S. Senate in Mississippi, speaks to media during a press conference at his campaign headquarters in Jackson, Miss. Wednesday, Oct. 14, 2020. During the press conference, Espy addressed his candidacy and Republican U.S. Senator Cindy Hyde-Smith's refusal to debate." data-c-credit="Eric Shelton/Clarion Ledger"></div></figure><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>"I think it is imperative that voters hear directly from Sen. Cindy Hyde-Smith, and directly from me, about where we stand on the important issues of Mississippi," Espy said, adding she is disrespecting Mississippi voters and "taking them for granted." </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p><strong class=gnt_ar_b_al>Their debate in 2018:</strong><a href=http://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/elections/2018/11/20/ms-sen-debate-what-cindy-hyde-smith-mike-espy-said-before-runoff/2012159002/ target=_blank rel=noopener data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>Scandals, health care, 'public hangings' and more: Key takeaways from #MSSen debate</a></p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>He said stark differences with Hyde-Smith is exactly why they should debate. "If you felt the same about views, programs or had a similar platform, you wouldn't have to debate anyone," Espy said. </p><aside aria-label=advertisement class="gnt_m gnt_x gnt_x__lbl gnt_x__al"><div data-g-r=lazy data-gl-method=lazyLoadX id=~ad-slot-7103-ms-jackson-C1098-native-article_link-news-politics-2 class="gnt_x_sl gnt_x_al"></div></aside><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Espy said the campaign received two debate invitations. A campaign spokeswoman said WJTV-TV and WLBT-TV both invited the candidates to separate debates. Espy agreed to a pair of dates, one in August and one in September, and said he is willing to attend one before Nov. 3. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p><strong>2019 </strong><a href=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/2019/06/13/mississippi-elections-why-do-top-governor-ag-candidates-dodge-debates/1418738001/ target=_blank rel=noopener data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a><strong>Debate dodgers:</strong> Top Mississippi candidates avoid debates. Why?</a></p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Hyde-Smith said the next few weeks are too busy. She said she will be back in Washington, D.C. early next week for much of the rest of the month due to the U.S. Supreme Court confirmation of Amy Coney Barrett. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>But Espy pointed out that other high-profile Senate Republicans had recently found time to debate their challengers — including Majority Leader Mitch McConnell of Kentucky, Lindsey Graham of South Carolina and Maine's Susan Collins.</p><figure class="gnt_em gnt_em_img"><img class=gnt_em_img_i style=height:529px data-g-r=lazy data-gl-src="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2018/11/07/PJAM/b1ce54b3-ea7a-4613-87fe-c8809f19551f-WickerHydeSMith.jpg?width=660&height=529&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp" data-gl-srcset="https://www.gannett-cdn.com/presto/2018/11/07/PJAM/b1ce54b3-ea7a-4613-87fe-c8809f19551f-WickerHydeSMith.jpg?width=1320&height=1058&fit=crop&format=pjpg&auto=webp 2x" decoding=async alt="U.S. senators Roger Wicker and Cindy Hyde-Smith celebrate with supporters of their campaigns at their shared election night party at the Westin hotel in downtown Jackson. Tuesday, Nov. 6, 2018."/><div class="gnt_em_img_ccw gnt_em_img_ccw__cap gnt_em_img_ccw__crd" data-c-caption="U.S. senators Roger Wicker and Cindy Hyde-Smith celebrate with supporters of their campaigns at their shared election night party at the Westin hotel in downtown Jackson. Tuesday, Nov. 6, 2018." data-c-credit="Sarah Warnock, Clarion Ledger"></div></figure><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Hyde-Smith argued she already debated Espy once in 2018, and little has changed since then regarding their positions. Voters are welcome to research her voting record, she said, both in the Senate and her previous stint in the Mississippi Legislature, to learn more about where she stands on issues. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>"I don't feel extremely compelled that the people of Mississippi think that it's really, really important," she said of a debate, adding it's "easy to see the differences" and labeling Espy as a liberal. She did not directly respond to a question about whether a debate might help voters better understand those policy differences. </p><aside aria-label=advertisement class="gnt_m gnt_x gnt_x__lbl gnt_x__al"><div data-g-r=lazy data-gl-method=lazyLoadX id=~ad-slot-7103-ms-jackson-C1098-native-article_link-news-politics-3 class="gnt_x_sl gnt_x_al"></div></aside><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Marvin King, an Ole Miss political science professor, said Hyde-Smith may fear giving Espy's campaign too much oxygen that could come along with a strong debate performance by him, or weak performance by her, so late in the race. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p><strong class=gnt_ar_b_al>Earlier:</strong><a href=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/2020/09/04/mississippi-senate-race-mike-espy-rally-stacey-abrams-jackson-church/5695664002/ target=_blank rel=noopener data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>Democrat Mike Espy holds first in-person rally of 2020 Senate campaign</a></p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>"It does deny swing voters — such that we have any in the state — the opportunity to see them on the same stage, answering the same questions," King said. </p><aside class="gnt_em gnt_em_anc" id=gnt_atomsnc data-g-r=lazy data-gl-method=loadAnc aria-label="Newsletter signup form"></aside><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Nathan Shrader, a Millsaps College political science professor, said it is highly unusual for a debate not to occur in a competitive Senate race. He said the sharply contrasting views Hyde-Smith described are the most important reason to hold a debate, because it allows the candidates to "lay that vision out, side by side." </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>Shrader said Hyde-Smith may be generally uncomfortable with debating after the <a href=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/elections/2018/11/20/ms-sen-debate-what-cindy-hyde-smith-mike-espy-said-before-runoff/2012159002/ target=_blank rel=noopener data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>2018 event against Espy</a>, which he said did not go well for her. She departed without answering reporters' questions and instead sent her colleague, Sen. Roger Wicker, to speak with the press about her performance. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p>"It's just not in her wheelhouse," Shrader said. </p><p class=gnt_ar_b_p><em>Contact Luke Ramseth at 601-961-7050 or <a href=mailto:lramseth@gannett.com data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>lramseth@gannett.com</a>. Follow <a href="https://twitter.com/lramseth?lang=en" data-t-l=|inline|intext|n/a class=gnt_ar_b_a>@lramseth</a> on Twitter.</em></p></div><div class=gnt_ss data-g-r=base_sc data-ss-u=https://www.clarionledger.com/story/news/politics/2020/10/15/hyde-smith-declines-debate-espy-mississippi-senate-race/3643690001/ data-ss-t="Espy wants a debate. Hyde-Smith doesn't. Will voters get to see the candidates before Nov. 3?" data-ss-d="U.S. Sen. Cindy Hyde-Smith said only &#34;losing candidates and reporters&#34; care about debates.
